  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6a7216a3-cb4a-4dd3-924b-9955cb3a9d3f'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer17385005584830962032"><b>Experience the wisdom of <i>Old Turtle<i>, the bestselling fable that explores society, the environment, and the spirituality they share.</i></i></b><br/>Who is God?<br/>Is He a wind that is never still?<br/>Is He a rock that never moves?<br/>Is He high above or here among us?<br/><br/>Venerable Old Turtle answers quietly: God is all of these things.<br/><br/><i>Old Turtle</i> first burst upon the publishing scene in 1992, and it was in</span>
  <span id="freeText17385005584830962032" style="display:none"><b>Experience the wisdom of <i>Old Turtle<i>, the bestselling fable that explores society, the environment, and the spirituality they share.</i></i></b><br />Who is God?<br />Is He a wind that is never still?<br />Is He a rock that never moves?<br />Is He high above or here among us?<br /><br />Venerable Old Turtle answers quietly: God is all of these things.<br /><br /><i>Old Turtle</i> first burst upon the publishing scene in 1992, and it was instantly recognized as a classic fable about ecology, peace, and the interconnectedness of all beings. Simple yet profound, it has since brought hope and inspiration to children and adults around the world.</span>

<div id="review_467604665" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/467604665" />
    <a title="Matthew Hunter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3040804-matthew-hunter"><img alt="Matthew Hunter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495642903p2/3040804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/467604665?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Hunter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Hunter" href="/user/show/3040804-matthew-hunter">Matthew Hunter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Adult leftists like me.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3040804-matthew-hunter?shelf=children-picture-books">children-picture-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer467604665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16268313573291398185">Douglas Wood visited our congregation last year. As part of a worship service, he read passages, sang, and played acoustic guitar while Cheng-Khee Chee's artwork cycled through on large screens in the sanctuary. The adult-heavy audience and worship setting were perfect, and absolutely beautiful. The emotionally evocative presentation of the award-winning children's book worked among liberal leaning, mainline Christian churchgoers. But as for the children? Well, let's just say the story and perfo</span>
  <span id="freeText16268313573291398185" style="display:none">Douglas Wood visited our congregation last year. As part of a worship service, he read passages, sang, and played acoustic guitar while Cheng-Khee Chee's artwork cycled through on large screens in the sanctuary. The adult-heavy audience and worship setting were perfect, and absolutely beautiful. The emotionally evocative presentation of the award-winning children's book worked among liberal leaning, mainline Christian churchgoers. But as for the children? Well, let's just say the story and performance set a mood conducive to a nap filled with sweet dreams. Despite the book's gentleness and beauty, there's not much in <i>Old Turtle</i> to captivate a young mind.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, I love <i>Old Turtle</i>! Cheng-Khee Chee's artwork is to die for. Wood's mystical and, in the end, hopeful take on conflict, diversity, divine mystery and environmental destruction speaks powerfully to me as a left-leaning clergyperson. But between the maturish message and subtle, softly lined artwork, I can't consider <i>Old Turtle</i> a children's book. A picture book for world federalists and universalists perhaps, but not for most little ones.<br /><br />Stick to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7784.The_Lorax" title="The Lorax by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lorax</a> if you want an environmental message presented in a vibrant and child-centered way. And you can't beat <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/773951.The_Story_of_Ferdinand" title="The Story of Ferdinand by Munro Leaf" rel="nofollow noopener">The Story of Ferdinand</a> as an example of gentleness in the face of violence.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16268313573291398185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2343881339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11527627485771394796">This is not a picture book for the very young, and, frankly, the "wise", vague exhortation to love those different from us--as we really are all one people--and listen to the messages from stones, plants, etc. is a bit precious, leaving me unmoved and unconvinced. While I don't quibble with the basic (unbroken) truth of the book that humanity is one, it would be refreshing to actually read a wise book that somehow communicated the extreme difficulty that sometimes (often?) exists when it comes t</span>
  <span id="freeText11527627485771394796" style="display:none">This is not a picture book for the very young, and, frankly, the "wise", vague exhortation to love those different from us--as we really are all one people--and listen to the messages from stones, plants, etc. is a bit precious, leaving me unmoved and unconvinced. While I don't quibble with the basic (unbroken) truth of the book that humanity is one, it would be refreshing to actually read a wise book that somehow communicated the extreme difficulty that sometimes (often?) exists when it comes to accepting and finding commonality with those whose ways are very different from ours! This is a "pretty" book--with flowery language and a sort of hushed and holy tone--that idealistic adults might like (it's much like Muth's The Three Questions, which I am also not a fan of) but I don't think it's a particularly great book for kids. If you prefer something a little more solid and truthful, and if you have problems with John Muth's other works, this story by Douglas Wood with illustrations by Muth won't be your cup of tea--as it wasn't mine.<br /><br />(By the way, how did Old Turtle end up with the other half of the broken truth, anyway? The other half supposedly "blazed off through the night sky". Is Old Turtle a flying turtle? This is what I mean about preciousness. I like poetic books, but this book just seemed to be silliness masquerading as wisdom!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11527627485771394796" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17330558879760879871" style="display:none">this was a nice book on diversity. i think one of the things people get the most worked up over is spirituality. it’s one of those things that can touch a person more deep than anything else, and everyone’s perspective will differ, even if only minutely. wars have been started over the issue, and all because we’re too pig headed and focused on our own validity. this book starts off with animals and rocks and trees each saying that what they think god is is indeed the true god, and that god seems to resemble the speaker. then the old turtle stops them and tell them of the coming of a new group, humans, and how they are supposed to be a message from god the the earth and a prayer from the earth to god. then people come and after while start to do not so nice things and nature says to stop. then the beings that said god was like themselves at the beginning of the book said they saw god in that which was opposite themselves. i guess the moral being have an open mind about that which is different from yourself, because it really isn’t so alien to what you believe.</span>

Today I need to find it on my shelf, and savor it again.<br/><br/>Read this for yourself, then read it to a child or two or even an entire classroom.<br/></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17537802567759981781">A 1993 American Booksellers Association Book of the Year and wonderful book for both children and adults. Through the text, words of the Old Turtle and other animals, and of images comes the story of meaning and of God. This book has been on my shelves for many years and I am very pleased to have now read it. It brought me peace and will be read again.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1905275019" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1905275019" />
    <a title="Bessana Kendig" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64365998-bessana-kendig"><img alt="Bessana Kendig" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485629238p2/64365998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1905275019?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bessana Kendig" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bessana Kendig" href="/user/show/64365998-bessana-kendig">Bessana Kendig</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64365998-bessana-kendig?shelf=wide-reading-columbia-38-2601">wide-reading-columbia-38-2601</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1905275019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16992860470716425103">Old Turtle written by Douglas Wood, is about a wildlife ecosystem that argues about who God is. They each have their own personal version of what they believe but Old Turtle's position is that God is in everything. When humans inherit the earth they fight and kill over their own beliefs in God and the Old Turtle helps them find peace and see God in beauty.<br/><br/>I give this story a three star rating. I feel like it is sentimental and beautiful but not altogether inclusive because no matter what, God ex</span>
  <span id="freeText16992860470716425103" style="display:none">Old Turtle written by Douglas Wood, is about a wildlife ecosystem that argues about who God is. They each have their own personal version of what they believe but Old Turtle's position is that God is in everything. When humans inherit the earth they fight and kill over their own beliefs in God and the Old Turtle helps them find peace and see God in beauty.<br /><br />I give this story a three star rating. I feel like it is sentimental and beautiful but not altogether inclusive because no matter what, God exists in this universe which demotes atheism. I know atheism is less common and the meaning of this book is larger than religion but it can also be viewed as too preachy and exclusive. <br /><br />"And often the people misused their powers, and hurt one another, or killed one another. And they hurt the earth. Until finally even the forests began to die..."(n.p.) this is some serious darkness entering the world which can either be because of arguments about God or because the people become godless. Either way, the message is clearly faith and hope are the strongest forces for positive impact. <br /><br />This story makes me feel like there is more of an open door for young people to choose spirituality over a specific belief system. Back when I was in school you were usually committed to whatever religion your parents worshipped, and it is somewhat the same these days, but this story reveals that there is more of a understanding that as long as there is a belief in something larger than oneself (not atheism) then you have faith and the ability to find hope throughout life. <br /><br />The classroom connection for this book could be the understanding that even when arguments arise and people see situations with very different perspectives they can find common ground with a positive platform. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16992860470716425103" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <a title="Josephine Briggs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/100597016-josephine-briggs"><img alt="Josephine Briggs" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3299055117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13450244781612597541">This is a beautiful book that words cannot begin to describe. I bought it a long time ago. A young man, an environmentalist recommended it. It is a wonderful book for children and for everyone. The artwork is beautiful and colorful. Old Turtle is so old, so intelligent, so knowing. This book won the Abby Book of the Year, 1993 Awards, Children's Book Awards, International Reading Association, American Booksellers Association. The book is short, not overly wordy, but tells so much.<br/><br/>Before mankind </span>
  <span id="freeText13450244781612597541" style="display:none">This is a beautiful book that words cannot begin to describe. I bought it a long time ago. A young man, an environmentalist recommended it. It is a wonderful book for children and for everyone. The artwork is beautiful and colorful. Old Turtle is so old, so intelligent, so knowing. This book won the Abby Book of the Year, 1993 Awards, Children's Book Awards, International Reading Association, American Booksellers Association. The book is short, not overly wordy, but tells so much.<br /><br />Before mankind came upon the earth, all spoke and understood one another. Then arguments began. Everything, fish stars wind, trees all said the God was with them only. Loud arguments. Then spoke Old Turtle, who rarely ever spoke. She said "God Is."<br /><br />There will be new families upon the earth, all different. Humans came and before long began arguing about God. People, who came from God forgot and began fighting, starting trouble, wars, ruining the earth God had given them. Came a voice. "Please Stop."<br /><br />And them remembered. <br />And Old Turtle smiled.<br />Excellent and beautiful book, to be read and remembered. </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aPLoZy1v2oolbAruJ1w6WkixutWYyi6kvZQLlXGZp1l9kw3MfIschZRXMSx3F2xh8c17DyfCVOXNBBuAD1f4iQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12693108310134558865">Composer, recording artist, wilderness guide, and self-taught naturalist-Douglas Wood is perhaps most widely known as the highly acclaimed author of OLD TURTLE, a 1993 ABBY Award winner and an International Reading Association Book of the Year. Author of several books for readers of all ages, Douglas says he is always seeking themes that are universally significant to both children and adults. His</span>
  <span id="freeText12693108310134558865" style="display:none">Composer, recording artist, wilderness guide, and self-taught naturalist-Douglas Wood is perhaps most widely known as the highly acclaimed author of OLD TURTLE, a 1993 ABBY Award winner and an International Reading Association Book of the Year. Author of several books for readers of all ages, Douglas says he is always seeking themes that are universally significant to both children and adults. His first book for Candlewick Press, GRANDAD'S PRAYERS OF THE EARTH-winner of the Christopher Medal for "affirming the highest value of the human spirit"-quietly explores the theme of grief and healing while celebrating a human connection to the natural world and the enduring spirit of love. Douglas Wood kept in mind someone very special to his own life when writing GRANDAD'S PRAYERS OF THE EARTH. "I feel I've been getting ready to write this book all my life, for it is about my wise and gentle hero, my Grandad. It's a prayer and a thank you, a walk in the woods, and a remembering smile; and it is for anyone who has ever had a woods to walk, a prayer to whisper, a hero to love." <br /><br /><br />Douglas Wood lives with his family in a log cabin on the banks of the Mississippi River in Minnesota.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12693108310134558865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
